B0067EKY7M|4.0|\\"Salmon Fishing in the Yemen\\" is a nicely-done British romantic comedy, built around a preposterous premise and the charm of two unlikely people falling in love.  Its very British humor won't appeal to everyone, but a strong cast sells the movie.<br /><br />When a wealthy Yemeni Sheik (an excellent Amr Waked) decides to build his own salmon fly-fishing stream in his desert homeland, government media expert Paula Maxwell (Kristen Scott Thomas) sees an opportunity for favorable publicity and pushes the project on skeptical Fisheries scientist Dr. Fred Jones (Ewan McGregor).  The reluctant Jones and hyper-efficient business consultant Harriet Chetwode-Tobin (Emily Blunt)begin to put flesh on the whimsical project, which takes on a life of its own, far up a narrow wadi in the Yemeni mountains.<br /><br />This is a fun movie with several narrative threads.  Maxwell's ruthless and hilarious quest for favorable publicity is one.  A second involves the troubled marriage of Dr. Jones and his careerist wife, and Harriet's stressful quickie wartime romance with a deployed British Army officer.  The main thread is the slow, uneven blossoming of a relationship between Fred and Harriet, as verbal sparring over a seemingly impossible project turns into a shared committment to something that might just work out.  A key scene comes early in the movie, over dinner in a Scottish castle, when the Sheik challenges the scientist's claimed lack of faith, using fishing as a telling metaphor.<br /><br />The movie has some jarring moments of excitement (the sheik has enemies) and some beautiful location shooting, including London, Scotland and Morocco (a stand-in for war-torn Yemen).  Best of all is the superb acting of McGregor and Blunt, putting their understated best into a touching romance.  \\"Salmon Fishing in the Yemen\\" is highly recommended as good entertainment for the patient viewer.

B002MQYOFW|5.0|Hunger Games stays true to the genre every step of the way.<br /><br />What always surprises me with books that take place in a distopian future, is that although the setting is somewhat detached and foreign to us, the characters remain staggeringly relatable. As a novel, Hunger Games does not belittle the reader by flattening the characters to fit into a group of narrow stereotypes - the brutish strongman, the foolish drunkard, the evil super villain. Peeta is a hopeless romantic, who is intelligent, strong, and charming, but absolutely hopeless at battle. Haymitch is neither a babbling drunk nor a secretly tormented genius. Even Cato, who could be argued to the worst type of person, mourns for the dying Clove.<br /><br />By comparison though, I must say the movie came a bit closer to oversimplification.<br /><br />Like other distopian societies, found in other futuristic books, Panem is a political commentary not on future events as they might unfold, but rather on current shortcomings that the author sees in society. The underlying theme is that a group of citizens who have been oppressed to the breaking point, come to see the idea of hope for a better future untenable. And upon giving up hope to change the harsh realities of their existence, these people grow desensitized to the violence of society around them, and actually become part of the problem themselves... at least it seems that this is what the author is trying to say.

B003O86FMW|3.0|To paraphrase a review from quite some time ago, one big problem with trilogies is the having to stick within the world you created part.  In your first book set someplace other than our real world, you're free to invent things -- so long as they make sense.  But once an audience has bought into your creations, you can't then contradict yourself or treat your new world any more sloppily than an actual historical setting.  So, if you're not sure how many books might follow, leave things open in your first book, then comb through those precedents when deciding what fresh challenges to throw at your characters in subsequent installments.<br /><br />Now, then: At the pivotal moment in The Hunger Games, Katniss and Peta strike what they surely HAD TO know was a stance of defiance against the Capitol: they agree to commit Romeo-and-Juliet style suicide, thus denying the Snow regime its authorized ending.  While this doesn't necessarily mean either is willing to become the face of the resistance, at the very least we now know that just as Peta didn't want to let the Games change him even before going in, Kat, too would now rather kill herself than play Snow's Games anymore.<br /><br />Senaca Crane has a heart and saves them -- and in so doing, shows a little backbone of his own, leading Snow to off him; this is the last scene of the movie, though Kat can't know this, as Snow admits until he pays her a threatening visit at the beginning of THIS book.  So far, so good.<br /><br />Suzaznne Collins' problem now is to thrust Kat, Peta, Gale, Prim, Mrs. Everdeen and even perhaps Buttercup into a believable NEW arena, not this year's version of the OLD one!!  Two Gamemakers with hearts of gold I can make myself believe, but as Kat muses in the midst of the first Games, though they DON'T ACTUALLY DO IT, the Capitol certainly COULD just outright kill a tribute in the arena; do you really believe Snow wouldn't handpick someone who would do just that this time his speech to Senaca about containing Kat's spark of hope last year having fallen on deaf ears??  No, this book should have been the time when Kat goes off-road, so to speak; she wouldn't even survive a Quarter Quell under these circumstances, let alone go on to become the Mockingjay afterward.<br /><br />What's more, don't you figure that if all of Panem knew that the Games held every 25th year were special in some way, they have been talking about it during the 74th Games, the ones Kat originally played in?<br /><br />Of course they would have.  And that's what I mean by having to respect your own world as an author.  If you don't create a complex and nuanced enough world to be able to dip back into for a plausible precedent in any subsequent installment you're going to have to weave something out of whole cloth when the time comes.  No matter how dramatic you make the \\"opening of the envelope\\" scene, readers WILL realize that its contents are no more a surprise to the producers of your Hunger Games than they are to, say the producers of Survivor.  If Snow wanted to kill Katniss, he could just as easily have her and Gale followed into the woods and shot by peacekeepers for poaching; why hold that ace in his hand when playing it wouldn't hurt his game in the least?  Oh yes, all Panem wants to see Kat married to Peta, but a regime as ruthless and firmly in control as Snow's could surely arrange a public double execution just as easily, solemly telling its crying subjects: \\"This is what happens when you defy us, your loving parents in government, and believe us when we say it hurts US more than it hurts you!\\"<br /><br />Would Panem really tune in to see old farts battle it out in slo-mo?  I know: Viewing is supposedly mandatory, at least in the Districts.  But that's yet another example of Collins asking us to suspend altogether too much disbelief for comfort, another problem with sequels in that there's a certain temptation toward laziness since you know those who loved your first book will at least buy and start your second.  Think about this, too: if that forcefield is strong enough to be used as a weapon, how can Kat's arrows and beatie's clever electricity trap possibly penetrate it?  For the last time, I say: Snow wouldn't underestimate Kat a second time -- especially not after the incident with the dress...<br /><br />So, three stars for effort.  If you just can't help yourself, get Catching Fire and look past all these implausibilities.  But if you merely LIKED The Hunger Games, you might want to sit this one (and also Mockingjay) out.ll at least buy and start your second. For the last time, I say: Snow wouldn't underestimate Kat a second time -- especially not after the incident with the dress...<br /><br />So, three stars for effort.  If you just can't help yourself, get Catching Fire and look past all these implausibilities.  But if you merely LIKED The Hunger Games, you might want to sit this one (and also Mockingjay) out.

I had no idea.\\" That makes for a good book, in my opinion.<br /><br />As a children's librarian, I would recommend this book to parents whose children are learning about China in school. The product's description that these images \\"break all the stereotypes of the Chinese\\" is spot-on. Children are able to get a very good view of a China that they are (most likely) not getting from school textbooks. I love the pictures of the children - when I show children who I work with what others are like in different cultures, showing them pictures of children like them really helps them to understand that there are children all over the world just like them.<br /><br />This book would be an excellent discussion-starter for parents who have adopted a child from China. A child can be exposed to their birth country through Carter's photographs. I would imagine families who were looking to adopt a child from China could also use this book to go deeper into understanding the country. Carter's photographs are up close, personal, and really make you feel like you've visit China.

B000W7JWUA|4.0|Decided to go out on a limb and try the table top game everyone has been talking about.  Boy am I glad I did!<br /><br />The rules were really simple to learn.  The board doesn't take long to set up and games take about 1.5 hours.  2 technically can play and learn the ropes, but the game is meant for 3-4 people.  Deciding where you start usually takes a bit, and decisions later can affect how the whole game will pan out.<br /><br />There is some strategy, but most of the game is based around the luck of the dice.  So if luck based games aren't for you I'd be a bit wary of Catan.  Me and my friends have fun with a game or two a night and leave it at that until next time.  Games can be frustrating if you're not winning - you could be stranded, blocked in and not getting resources for the longest time; and if people aren't willing to trade there's little incentive to keep playing.<br /><br />Overalll, Catan is a great beginner's table top game and a lot of fun!

0761169253|5.0|Just spent less than an hour reading a great book.  Yes, I'm biased. It was written by my nephew.  \\"Steal Like An Artist,\\" by Austin Kleon, is for anybody who is, was or will be stuck in their own creative neurosis, unable to accept their giftings, unable to move forward, unable to risk failure.  Perhaps what I love most about the book is the surprisingly practical advice it offers to creative types from a young man I view as a creative genius. I didn't expect this ultra-deep thinking melancholy, whom I've watched grow up (albeit from a distance), to offer such wonderfully useful instruction.  The book, which has quickly made the New York Times best-seller list for advice books, is also amazingly spiritual. Full of subtle but sound biblical encouragement (which I'm pretty sure was unintentional), this easy-reading, 140-page work could easily be the basis of a small-group (Bible?) study. And before the religious Pharisees of our day start railing about how the title defies the eighth commandment, please just save it. (You'd do well to heed the encouragement of Bishop Joseph Garlington of Covenant Church of Pittsburgh - one of the great pastors of our day - who openly acknowledges that when he hears a great nugget from other pastors or spiritual leaders, he won't hesitate to steal it, though he'll give credit the first time.)  With chapter titles like \\"Don't Wait Until You Know Who Are To Get Started,\\" \\"Use Your Hands,\\" \\"Do Good Work and Share it With People\\" and \\"Be Nice,\\" the advice is in some ways a handbook for living out life as God designed us to do.  I already have at least 10 people I have in mind who need to read this book. I'll be placing my order shortly.  Years ago when Austin first created his website [...], I told his mom that a day would come when people would discover him - that his work would one day have a wider audience. It's exciting for me to see that happening.  What's perhaps most exciting for me is to see how grounded Austin is. It's very easyfor creatives to get lost and detached in their own creativity. Clearly that hasn't happened with Austin. Of course, I credit God - and a praying grandmother - for that influence, which I'm certain will continue to bear fruit for years to come.  Good job, Austin. I'm proud of you.  To order the book, click Austin's website link here. Austin, who lives in Austin, Texas, with his wife, Meghan, will be in Cleveland, Ohio, on June 9 as part of his \\"Steal Across America\\" book tour. Check it out if you get a chance. B005WGBQ9G|5.0|Okay first off, the story line and progression is slow because its a DRAMA. When i was suspended from school, and stayed at home and watched tv, i was stuck with watching soaps because we couldnt afford cable, and many of those dramas where sloooooww....So that brings me to this show, yeah its going to be slow, and i appreciate that, too many shows are fast paced and character development happens way too soon. I've seen all of the first and second season, and the show catches me off guard like no other. Some characters are obvious like Shane, but others like Andrea, to go from a weak suicidal person, to a stronger more independant woman was unseen. I figured Andrea would stay her suicidal self. Next comes Carl, a young boy who has seen way too much and gone through alot, he could have remained a weak character, but as the days go by he steels his mind.<br /><br />Now to the comment about why Rick leting Carl approach the deer. Its common knowledge to never approach wild life in areas with potiential hunters, but heres the thing, its the mother loving apocalypse, they, including myself, would not exactly expect many hunters in the area, and regardless of Carl approaching the deer with the potential of a hunter, there's ALSWAYS that risk factor of a walker springing up and biting him. With that said, him approaching that deer was symbolic. It was an opportunity for Carl to see something that was beautiful in a world gone to hell. If i were a father, and I had my kid with me, and they saw a deer and had a chance to interact with it, I would give my kid that chance because who knows when he or she will ever get to see the wonders of life, when all this kid has seen is death.<br /><br />For the characters acting \\"stupid\\" its SURVIVAL, like many have pointed out there are 2 police officers, they're the only ones who has been through life or death situations prior to the walkers. Many of you can think \\"im ready for an zombie scenario\\" but your not. You may have the equipment on standby, like shelters and bug out bags, but unless you've been in a life or death situation already (survival situation) then your not ready. Do yourself a favor and get out of denial because any army vetren (such as my father), will tell you that all your preparidness will be worth nothing unless you've been in a survival situation. A common person, such a lawyer, cashier, ect. will most likely act stupid, more or less because they havent had the slightest clue what to do without the norms of society.<br /><br />So unless all the characters are from the police department, military, national guard or any job that puts that persons life on the line on a day to day basis, I foresee the characters making bad decisions or being \\"stupid\\". People do dumb things when their scared and panicked.<br /><br />To those of you who are my age (21) and younger, we come from a fast pace, instant gratification generation. But we gotta stop that crap, and slow it down, and remember that this is a drama. I appreciate this show because of its pace, I love watching old 2-3 even 4 hour long westerns where story line developes very slowly, I even like slow movies like the Big Lobowski. So learn to appreciate the pace, because if this show gets too fast paced like yall are wishing for...well your just going to dislike the show because it will turn into a mindless action flick. I honestly think this show brings back what alot of hollywood has lost. There are way too many cut and paste shows, I actually feel like im watching a unique show, rather than some clone with new names.
